Free Talk

On the Form of Poetry 319

— Chen Junhan

Poetry is a product of society.

The most important issue in poetry is the content and the form. I have always believed that the consistency of content and form is an absolutely unbreakable topic. It is generally believed that this kind of consistency presupposes contradiction and is incompatible. But this is a mistake. Literature must explain that the law of literature is whole, a social function, a special superstructure, but its explanation must include the question of form.

The form I am talking about here has nothing to do with formalism. The theory of formalism is closely related to formalist art. The most important mistake of formalism is that it separates art from the complexity of modern society. The analysis of form is indeed useful and indispensable, but formalists regard it as an unquestionable truth.

In order to demand consistency between the content and form of a work, we cannot ignore the issues of heritage inheritance and proficient artistic skills. Then we must ask how we can learn from past masters or ancient books? To answer this question, we must know that negation is not a simple process of destruction, but a form of rebirth. Hegel said it well, "The ancients existed in existing forms." Although inheritance is possible, destruction is actually inevitable.

Now, if we review the poetry of the past and compare it with the great content of real life, then the content of poetry is bleak. Our poetry has not yet reached a level that can understand the entire significance of our era.

Therefore, we cannot ignore the subject matter of poetry. That is to say, the subject matter in poetry must be suitable for the complexity of our era and all its contradictions. Taking subject matter from this point of view will achieve consistency.

If we need a variety of poetic materials, it is not difficult to understand that, according to the combination of form and content, a variety of poetic forms are necessary.

The rhythm of an elegy cannot be the same as the rhythm of a military song, because the reaction of the image is also the content of its emotions. However, if we admit that a variety of poetic materials are appropriate, the result is a variety of poetic forms. In such a situation, what is the driving force of formal consistency? If there is true consistency between form and content, then the consistency of subject matter must be in harmony with the consistency of form, which goes without saying. This repeated consistency will be obtained through consistency of style or consistency of method.

The forms created by poetry should be diverse. Their consistency comes from the same great style or from the social realist method.

Recently, Mr. Yu Dafu's talk about poetry mentioned new and old poems. According to his opinion, whether new poetry can be established is still a question, and even teaches people not to do it; as for old poetry, according to the historical procedure, "as long as Chinese characters do not change, fashionable young people wearing Western clothes and drinking brandy will definitely hum some five-character and seven-character verses to pass the time." The person who wrote this article completely ignored the issue of consistency between the content and form of poetry; he only expressed his narrow prejudice.

Old Partner 320

— Zigang

Like magpies who love to build new nests and can't live on a tree for half a month, I am also such a restless guy, always dreaming of soaring through the sky, so I live everywhere for a month or so. Fortunately, it's so easy for a single person to move.

Recently, I carried my net basket and bedding into the empty backyard of this old house again. The bald trees and dead grass in the yard made people feel refreshed, although I couldn't see flowers or fruits. It was the gloomy demon king driving away the winter of the world.

At night, when I opened my bedding and spread it on the ground alone under the lamp, I suddenly heard a few coughs from the empty rooms a few rooms to the south, as if it took a lot of effort. After coughing, I hummed. It was clearly an old man. But I remembered that those rooms were empty, so I shivered one after another. Wrapped in the quilt, I thought of the fox fairies that people usually talked about. Fox fairies live in quiet corners, with white beards hanging from their cheeks, shaking their furry tails as they walk, coughing lightly.

That night, I dreamed of a group of big foxes and little foxes with a foxy smell.

The next morning, I ran to the outer courtyard to inquire with the tenants there.

"A retired soldier lives there. Don't be afraid. He's very kind," she added, "The might of a soldier will be gone with the military uniform he takes off."

When I returned to the backyard with peace of mind, an old man with a hunched back was standing under the steps of the south house, watering a pot of tender green bamboo with a mouthwash cup. One empty hand was still stroking the quietly unfolding clear green leaves. There really was a beard hanging down, but its color was gray.

In order to avenge my night of fright, I also coughed softly without warning. He raised his head in response and straightened his back. He was still a burly figure. Half a scar crawled out from under his small felt hat. His direct gaze revealed his sincerity.

I smiled, and he smiled back, his eyelids twitching slightly.

"Do you live in the south house?"

His voice was quite heavy and turbid, with a Shanxi accent: "Yes, did you move in yesterday? That's good. This yard is so quiet that even ghosts are about to dare to live here."

"I heard you coughing last night and thought a fox fairy had come."

He laughed heartily, stroking his silver-gray beard that resembled a rainy sky. Then he asked about my origin and school, sighing endlessly for those who were away from home. Because we were both wandering outside, we became familiar more quickly.

"I have a granddaughter as old as you!"

So, I had one more grandfather in name.

This old man loved to talk about trivial matters before and after his life, as well as his dead deeds. To him, these were as precious as his own life. They were indeed the deep scars of the life he had dragged through!

He often talked about the battles he had fought in the army. He was a small pawn of the warlord ××, but he wasn't that small. In the year after he took a bullet, he became a platoon leader and led troops.

"Look, a piece of meat was dug out of my leg, a piece of flesh was shaved off my shoulder, and the scar under my hat caused illness. It aches on cloudy days. Damn it, my ancestors didn't accumulate virtue by being soldiers!" He blinked his eyes, clenched his fist, and sighed. I often make fun of his habit of blinking.

"It was all熬出來守着通夜 or rolling around in the trenches. Sometimes, my eyes were so red that they were about to bleed, but I was still aiming my gun. How much worse is this life than yours studying? Your textbooks don't necessarily record the names of the brothers who risked their lives, do they?"

I told him that they did, but they were only the names of their marshals or generals. He smiled bitterly:

When he talked about his family members, the old man would tell people in a hoarse voice that his cousin was killed while standing on the side of his enemy, regretting:

"It's incomprehensible. Two brothers who used to catch crickets together in their hometown ended up fighting each other."

The old man lived his days on the small allowance his daughter sent him every month. His eyesight was failing, and his hands and feet would cramp from time to time. On sunny days, he would move a small stool and sit in the chaotic open space on the north side to bask in the sun, watching the light of the black cat's pupils crawl into the house to prepare his own meal on a small stove. Sometimes, when I came home from school, the old man would smile and offer me a pancake or half a cornbread. When I praised his good craftsmanship, he would be happy.

"I haven't eaten a meal cooked by my own wife in three years. By the time I retired, she had already entered the grave!"

Stroking my short hair, the old man would pout and talk about his granddaughter:

"She grows vegetables outside the city. She doesn't have her hair cut so short. Her braids are very long."

The other day, when the child came to send money to her grandfather, I happened not to be there. When I came back, the old man happily told me when his real granddaughter was coming to see me, the one with the hat mark.

Sometimes I would run to the old man's room to chat with him and drink a cup of light tea from his clay teapot. He was very happy to have the opportunity to chat about everything under the sun. Many times, he gently chided my habit of moving.

"Just stay here. Isn't it very pleasant?"

I also became docile:

"Okay, I'll stay here, old partner… no, Grandpa."

Silence 321

— Zheng Guanghan

Living as a modern person, most people know some of the benefits of silence, but few people can diligently practice it. The wise Israeli King Solomon (Solomon) said ten centuries ago, "The mouth of the wise is hidden in his heart, but the heart of the fool is hung on his mouth." This sentence is indeed worth pondering. Many people often see things that others find pleasing to the eye, but they simply can't stand, and as a result, they voluntarily break the commandment of "silence" and bring a lot of trouble. According to Solomon, they are just big fools. The wise hide their mouths in their hearts, so naturally there is nothing to say; everyone has nothing to say, and the atmosphere is peaceful, isn't that good? But some fools come out and want to hang their hearts on their mouths, chattering endlessly, saying a lot of discouraging words. Although the words have been said, and perhaps said very loudly, it is a pity that this world can only lose them forever.

Two thousand five hundred years ago, the great Greek philosopher Pythagoras taught the world: "Close your mouth, or say something more valuable than silence." The words of a bookworm seem reasonable at first glance, but on closer reflection, they can't help but feel foolish: to distinguish what words are valuable and what words are worthless is already a difficult problem at present. Do people really say words that have no value at all? I think, if they knew in the underworld, they would not agree. The Bible does not sing praises to those warriors who "take a city," but praises those wise men who can "rule their own spirit," and this is not without reason. There are many words in the world that, when spoken, make people "sincerely convinced," but they don't say them, preferring to leave them for the wise to say, and they prefer to say words that "seek suffering for themselves." No matter how many such tragic facts have occurred in history, people still do not know to be vigilant, and still prefer to endure torture for being talkative, and even sacrifice themselves. I am amazed at why there are so many "fools" in this world.

In the middle of the night, I wake up from a dream and think of a few friends who gathered together day and night two or three years ago. Now some of them have passed away, and some are wandering in various places with unknown fates. I can't help but sigh repeatedly. St. Francis (St. Francis) said, "It is better to be silent than to speak the truth in an 'unhumorous' way, otherwise, it would be like pouring bad soy sauce on a good dish." Now, many clever people have learned to avoid the directness of truth and specialize in writing from the side, which can avoid suspicion and allow readers to relax, which is extremely clever. It's just a pity that some people can neither remain silent nor understand the way to add that dish of "soy sauce." What to do? What to do?

The Last Sadness (Part 2) 322

— Mo Qing

Ah, I have been so tired and weak these days! I have traveled thousands of miles by water and stayed in countless strangers' homes. I have had sleepless nights of terror. I have also had days when countless needles seemed to be pricking my brain all day long. I have even had endless days of nonstop, hoarse work. Alas, don't these weak nerves and this tired body need some rest? It's time. Why not let me sleep quietly for a moment, even just for a moment.

Yesterday morning, I took the opportunity to run to the French Park. Standing in the towering pavilion at the intersection of Avenue Dubail, I leaned on the railing and stood there in a daze for a long time. The leaves on the treetops of the not-so-sparse forest of French parasol trees in the park had almost fallen. Along the creek, there were a few poplars that could withstand the cold, with only slender, withered, and yellow willow branches remaining. When the cold wind blew, even people with tough hearts would be quietly moved! The water in the stream was fanned up with gentle ripples, passing all the way through the bridge. The lake was tightly locked with wrinkles, and it was even more difficult to resolve its sorrow. There were very few visitors in the morning. Ah! This park full of rustling sparse forests, this park full of flying fallen leaves, this park full of sorrowful waters, accompanied by the weeping of the flowing spring falling from the mountain peak, was enough to break one's heart. This scene suddenly reminded me of many old things at the Yellow Crane Tower and on the top of Snake Mountain. Ah, I am afraid to think deeply, and I am even more afraid to watch for a long time!

I shifted my gaze to the vague and hazy horizon. What immediately caught my eye were those deformed, round, and square buildings with more than ten or dozens of stories. Ah, I finally realized that I had drifted to the largest metropolis in East Asia. Ah, look: the sky is full of thick black lines, and the ground is full of madly running monsters of civilization. These high-voltage currents sending waves, these spherical axles, these thunderstorms made of metal. All these electric vehicles and gasoline vehicles are moving around and fighting. Ah, this is the manifestation of power, the manifestation of machinery, the manifestation of hard steel. Since I am in this tense and sharp environment, how can I allow myself to withdraw so weakly and stand aside to seek sorrow and express emotion? Ah, if I can't roll up my sleeves and angrily jump into this group of power struggles to learn to hone myself, then I'm afraid I won't be crushed into meat paste when a storm comes!

However, tonight, terrible sadness has once again crept into my heart! Ah, my body has felt an unstoppable cold, and my belly has felt an unbearable hunger. If I can't become a little harder, I tell you: I will roll up my sleeves and stride into the group of hard power struggles. Ah, you terrible sadness, you ugly sadness, please get out of here! With a somersault, get out of here forever!

Late November night, early morning of December in Shanghai.

Dear Mr. Ah San... 323

Smile (1) 324

— Written by Lawrence of England, translated by Tang Xiru

He was determined to sit up all night as a kind of penance. The telegram simply said: "Ophelia is critically ill." He thought that in this situation, it would be too inhumane to go to the sleeping car to sleep. So when the night covered France, he was still sitting wearily in the first-class carriage.

Of course, he should have been sitting by Ophelia's bedside long ago, but Ophelia didn't want him, so now he was sitting in the carriage.

In the depths of his heart, there was a black, heavy weight: like a poisonous tumor pregnant with absolute darkness, pulling his heart straight down. He had always taken life very seriously, and now seriousness overwhelmed him. His dark, handsome, clean-shaven face, and his deeply worried, slanted, thick black eyebrows could really be used to make a statue of Christ on the cross.

The night in the car was like a hell: nothing was real. The two old English women opposite him had already died. Perhaps they had died before he died, because, of course, he regarded himself as dead.

He felt the slow, gray light of dawn crawling up from the many mountains on the border. At the same time, his heart was repeatedly chanting: —

"When the dawn comes with the early morning rain,

Dark, melancholy, and cold.

Her peaceful eyelids closed:

She has another morning that is not ours."

His monk-like, unchanging face of suffering did not reveal even a trace of the contempt, and self-contempt, that his keen heart determined was present in this thought that was initially serious and then harmonious.

He was in Italy. He looked at this country with a faint disgust. When he saw the olive trees and the sea, he only felt a kind of disgust and could no longer feel anything else. It was all a poetic deception.

Relief from Melancholy or Relief from Oneself 325

— Chen

The "disease of the times" for young people — melancholy — Mr. Bing published his new views in the 7th issue of this publication. Bing said that the source of most young people's melancholy is not due to "the disturbances of the world, the darkness of society, the fall of human relationships," because after they have been in society for some time, they feel that it doesn't matter. But melancholy still covers their hearts, so they need to seek answers from themselves. And Bing concluded by quoting Yuan Zhonglang's words as a reasonable method of remedy, saying that there must be a spiritual sustenance: "taking chess as a sustenance, taking sex as a sustenance, taking skill as a sustenance, taking writing as a sustenance."

There is a traditional Chinese thought that when the world is in turmoil, people want to seek a paradise. Tao Yuanming's "The fields are about to be overgrown, why not return?", Zhuge Liang's leisurely life in Wolonggang, all belong to this kind of "Everyone is drunk, I am the only one sober; everyone is turbid, I am the only one pure." Laughing at the wind and moon, drinking and composing poetry, is indeed an eternal anecdote and a name that will be remembered in the universe.

This trend has been passed down to the present and is still a kind of "national essence," so in the midst of shouts of killing, we have discovered things like "drinking bitter tea and planting sesame." But there are too many young people who are "busy all year round as if they have lost something," so people who are good at expressing their emotions have brought out Yuan Zhonglang to persuade people to express their emotions in chess, sex, skill, writing, etc., to prosper the world. It seems that these things can cure the disease of young people's melancholy, just like a "panacea," with unexpected effects. Bing's remarks about relieving young people's melancholy are based on this idea.

The ability of hypnosis to cure diseases lies in its ability to numb people's nerves: and the ability of expressing emotions in chess, sex, skill, and writing to relieve young people's melancholy lies in the spiritual sustenance, the two actually have the same effect. Monks, nuns, hermits, celebrities, and Yuan Zhonglang are all worthy of envy and praise, and the meaning is probably in this. However, Bing said that expressing emotions in chess, sex, skill, and writing can "live their lives happily, and achieve higher attainments," otherwise they will frown all day long and live a miserable life without tasting a bit of the sweetness of life, which is indeed beyond imagination.

However, I don't know if young people in general take this as a guide. After "expressing emotions" in chess, sex, skill, and writing to make their spirits have sustenance and relieve their melancholy, whether they still have to eat and live, and when suffering is still unavoidable, it will still make people "busy all day long as if they have lost something." If emotions can be expressed and life can be happy, and attainments can be high, it is really too good, too good: the melancholy of "worrying for no reason and not being happy in the face of beauty" is indeed "pitiable, pitiable," so in order to realize this idea, it is best to have not only a spiritual sustenance, but also a physical sustenance, that is, no longer having to eat and live, and relieving oneself.

An Unmarried Woman 326

— Hu Weixiong

From a pile of New Year's cards, I discovered a small violet note:

Old friend, I have no other New Year's greetings for you, I hope you will wait for me at the Grand Theater at nine o'clock tonight, you certainly know who is writing the letter.

This day last year, I also received a violet note like this, with only the four words "Happy New Year" on it. From my vague memory, it was certainly written by the same person, but I couldn't be sure if this letter writer was joking among friends, or some kind of mysterious event?

I was preoccupied with this thought, it seemed that all the friends I met today were suspicious, especially when they mentioned going to the Grand Theater to see a movie. I exhausted all kinds of methods to probe every suspect, but to no avail.

When evening came, I prepared to go to the Grand Theater to make a big joke.

Tonight, the audience was particularly crowded. In front of the ticket counter, groups of people were piled up, scrambling, as if the money in their hands couldn't be exchanged for a ticket. Although there were a few leisurely wandering in front of the door, I didn't run into any familiar faces.

Since I didn't necessarily want to see a movie, I was too lazy to compete in front of the ticket counter. Looking at the clock on the Hua'an Building from afar, it had just struck half past eight, so I stood nonchalantly in front of the door watching the people welcoming the New Year's arrival.

With my hands in my pockets, I stood like this for more than ten minutes, when someone patted me on the shoulder. Turning my head, it was an unfamiliar woman, but she opened her mouth to ask me:

"Do you know the person who asked you to wait?"

"Who are you?"

"If you received my letter, you'd know who I am."

She smiled triumphantly. I then remembered that she was my middle school classmate, Luo Lan, who I had parted ways with nearly ten years ago.

"Still acting like a child." I shook her hand tightly, expressing a kind of enthusiasm beyond gratitude.

"This way, it's a bit more interesting."

Inside, she told me that she had already come in the afternoon to buy tickets. When she came just now, she walked past you, and seeing that you didn't seem to recognize me, I stood by the window watching your actions. Later, I determined it was you. If I hadn't greeted you, it would have been quite interesting.

Sitting in the dark movie theater, we mumbled about what had happened since we parted.

Here, I must mention that we had been in love in school, but I failed. So, when we talked about marriage, she asked me if I was married. I playfully replied:

"The women I loved all ran away!! What about you?"

"The men I loved all ran away!"

We laughed softly, as if pulled back to the happy days of being students ten years ago.

After the show ended, we were reluctant to separate immediately. We strolled slowly on the sidewalk. Although it was winter, the wind blowing in our faces didn't feel cold. I suddenly thought of last year's New Year's card and said to her:

Page 20

"Who said it wasn't me who sent it?" she replied.

"How did you know what company I was at?"

"Have you flipped through our school's alumni directory?"

"Then, how did you think of this man who ran away?"

"It's nothing, I just thought of it occasionally."

We parted ways like this.

The next day, I found that violet note again:

Old friend, do you think this is really a coincidence? I hope you will muster the courage you had when you failed before. This time, victory is yours!

Widow 327

— Bo'er

Everyone in Xia Village knows that Sister-in-law Yi is a newlywed widow. Her beautiful face, her gentle demeanor, and her pleasing smile never fail to attract attention and praise. Everyone says: Yi's mother has good fortune to have taken such a beautiful daughter-in-law.

The sun shines on the peaceful village, and they all live carefree lives. But in recent years, it seems that everything has turned upside down. In addition, there is this war, the conscription of laborers. These things seem insignificant to the simple and brave young man, A Yi. He slowly and resolutely strides forward, and his shadow disappears from then on, never turning back to bid farewell to his wife of just over a month.

One day, two days, one month, two months, they still do not wait for A Yi to return.

At dusk, she quietly walks out of the city gate, stands on the bank of the De River, gazing at the distant, swaying boats approaching. She thinks: "Maybe that's him?" But the small boat passes her by without a second thought. Sister-in-law Yi's heart gradually darkens, because her disappointment has been accumulating for years, not just today. Every morning when she wakes up, she still remembers her husband's odd habits: having breakfast before brushing his teeth, putting on his hat before putting on his clothes. Now, everything is empty and quiet. That pleasing smile will no longer appear on her face. Occasionally, she tries to please her mother-in-law, and she forces a smile, but it provokes Yi's mother's resentment and curses: "What a jinx! A flesh-eating monster! What a waste of your extraordinary appearance..." Sister-in-law Yi has grown accustomed to hearing these things.

Sister-in-law Yi, with her wounded and haggard appearance, supporting her worried expression, carries a small bamboo basket. Following the rising sun, she goes to the morning market, buys the small crucian carp that her mother-in-law wants to eat, and some other vegetables. For months, it has become her habit. She carries the vegetable basket back before Yi's mother gets up.

Yi's mother says: "Why do you always buy this small crucian carp? Does the fish seller have a connection with you? Hmm..."

"If mother-in-law doesn't want to eat this, I'll buy something else tomorrow," Sister-in-law Yi answers cautiously and respectfully.

At this time, Little Pig runs in and says:

"Yi's mother! Yi's mother! Uncle Xia San from the market just passed by here. He asked if you were home. And who else is at home? I told him that you are often home, and then he ran away without saying anything."

Little Pig is an ignorant child who lives next door to Yi's mother. He likes to bring outside news to Yi's mother the most. This time, he told her what Xia San said, just as he usually does. Little did he know that Yi's mother had already cast her fierce gaze upon Sister-in-law Yi, holding her breath, standing up, heavily knocking on the table, and shouting loudly: "Good! You... shameless thing, he's coming to find you, go! Flesh-eating ancestor demon, don't you dare ruin my family's reputation! Get out of here!"

Sister-in-law Yi was about to speak up and explain, but her mother-in-law immediately shouted loudly! "What are you trying to argue?"

She didn't make a sound until the next morning. Yi's mother still didn't hear any sound from her daughter-in-law. She suspected that she was trying to upset her, but the truth told her that Sister-in-law Yi's body was already in the well.

Time Flies 328

— Ye Fei

The faint sun shines diagonally on the hillside. Old Grandpa A Qi sits on a green stone in front of the door, smoking his pipe with one puff and then none. He squints his old, blurred eyes, as if deep in thought. Two yellow bean-sized clear snot droplets hang on his few gray whiskers.

"Ping! Pang!" A group of children are setting off small firecrackers in the open space, wearing bright red and green new clothes, laughing and jumping happily. The surrounding air is filled with joy. His grandson, Yu'er, is also in the group, but he is not wearing new clothes. He is still wearing the same dirty, tattered padded jacket that he wears every day.

Ah! New Year's was such a happy time in childhood! But when one reaches middle age, especially old age, festivals or New Year's not only become bland, but sometimes evoke feelings of sadness and tears!

As he thinks, looking at this group of happy little angels, he can't help but think of his own childhood, and his son A Jin's childhood. In his own childhood, it was when his father was prominent in the village, so he had plenty of food and clothing, and lived without worries. The family hired two farmhands and a nanny. His father would hold a pipe and walk out the door with a small braid, and people would always call him "Second Master." When his son A Jin was a child, things were not as good as in the past! The family did not have to worry about food and clothing, but in the end, if you didn't work, you wouldn't eat. Unlike his father, when the rice was eaten, people would send rent rice, and when money was needed, people would bring it to the door. Now, things are even worse. Natural disasters and man-made calamities have struck one after another, and exorbitant taxes have been constantly increasing. Rural bankruptcy has reached its peak. The harvest of the year, including barley and corn, is not even enough to last until the next harvest. Not long after the flood, banditry and locust plagues broke out. Last year, there was even a drought. We poor people have no way to survive!

Even as he thinks like this, the fire in his pipe has gone out, but he still keeps desperately puffing away, making the pipe squeak...

Ai! I've lived for seventy or eighty years, and it's the first time I've encountered such a year. How can we get through such days? I've lived enough. Living longer would only waste food, but A Jin's days are really hard! The harvest is so scarce, but the burden is heavier every day. Other families play and have fun on the first day of the Lunar New Year, but he still went to the radish field last night to dig a load of radishes, and this morning he took them out to sell again. But now radishes are not worth much. In previous years, we could get more than a dozen silver dollars from this radish field, but now we can only sell them for five cents a pound. A load of radishes can't even be exchanged for one and a half liters of rice. How can our family of five survive!

As Old Grandpa A Qi was lamenting to himself, Mr. Wu came back from the teahouse in town, excited after drinking Yuanbao tea. Passing by here, he saw Old Grandpa A Qi sitting there alone, so he made a bow to him.

"Congratulations on getting rich! Grandpa A Qi, why don't you go to the tea house and sit at home alone on the first day of the Lunar New Year? Aren't you lonely?"

"Get rich! You get rich too! You came back from town early?" Old Grandpa A Qi reluctantly bowed slightly.

"The town is very quiet this year, it doesn't feel like the New Year at all. I wasn't interested in sitting there, and the gambling den didn't attract anyone either, so I went back to sleep."

"Ah! In such a year, we can't even fill our stomachs, so how can we have the mood to celebrate the New Year?"

"Don't you know! I heard that Chengtai, Xiangsheng, and several other stores have closed down, and I'm afraid some others won't be able to open!" Mr. Wu said as he walked away.

"If no one buys anything, the stores will naturally have a hard time opening!" Old Grandpa A Qi watched Mr. Wu's back disappear into the woods with a pair of melancholy eyes.

The Man Who Bears the Cross 329

— Green Silk

During the day, rubbing his sleepy eyes, he bids farewell to the darkness. As the morning rooster crows for the first time, and the stars have just disappeared into the blue sky, people of all classes stretch their lazy bodies.

The sky is a terrifying azure, like a blue snakeskin stretched across the sky.

The scene of early winter is indescribably desolate!

Every day, early in the morning, whipped by life, he jumps awake from a sweet dream, rubs his eyes, washes his face, puts on his clumsy clothes, and hurriedly slips out of the triangular little house that resembles the multi-lined homes of artists from ancient Greece and Rome.

Continuing, continuing to be loaded into the workplace, thirty li outside the city, and being driven back every day at twelve o'clock.

In the long-term, unceasing work, he bears the heavy cross according to his original will.

He never utters a sound of "tiredness," nor of "complaint," quietly following the turning of the great wheel of time, with the same inner and outer peace.

A beautiful soul, a noble and attractive figure, as if that kind of life has subdued him, even though he himself has never uttered a word of "disobedience."

The greatness lies in his calm and thoughtful manner, which is a rare type of person among those I have seen.

(Life is a symphony of joy and pain, and the ability to remain calm under great stimulation is what makes a person successful!)

Many times, when I felt empty and succumbed to negativity over trivial matters, he would always encourage me with those words!

(Women have no careers. How many great women have you seen, past and present, domestic and foreign?)

He sighs deeply, filled with infinite sadness.

(But, the morning rooster is singing, and the sun is rising from the east, and that is the light of hope!)

Words of warmth slip out from his curved lips, one by one.

(You understand me, but you have no way to fulfill my wish. Therefore, my emptiness dominates my entire life.)

Another pair of tears of gratitude rolls down her cheeks. She looks once more at the calm face of the man who bravely bears the cross, and her heart is filled with a deeper sense of indescribable shame and anxiety.

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Film Special

A Brief History of Film Development (4) 335

— Wen Ying

(4) The Origin of the "Star System"

At that time, when we talked about "stars," we only knew they were bright, shining things in the sky at night. How could those small-time capitalists who risked everything to invest in a five-cent movie theater imagine that those glittering things in the sky would sing, dance, walk, and eat on the ground? Indeed, at that time, there were already famous actors and actresses on the stage. Gentlemen and ladies wore formal attire, black overcoats, and tall hats, paying a high price to see Maude Adams, Mrs. Fiske, Edward Sothern, and others. How could they have imagined that these wealthy people would soon flock to small alleys, spending five cents to watch flickering shadows on a screen?

At that time, the "moving people" in movies were insignificant. They were not even as valuable as the projectors in small movie theaters. The producers at that time – in fact, they didn't even deserve the title of producer – would just grab anyone and put them in front of the camera, telling them to do this or that. They never imagined that these people would one day be more valuable than the cameras themselves. There was a woman named Gladys Smith who, after her husband died in Canada, was so poor that she had no food to eat. She took her three children to perform in plays to earn a living. Because performing in plays wasn't enough to support the family, the eldest daughter, named Gladys, went to a film company (Biograph Studio) in New York, hoping to earn a little more money to support her family. At that time, she used the name Mary Pickford. Little did she know that she would later become world-famous, known to every man, woman, and child!

At that time, film companies could not hire famous stage actors. The big names on the stage called this new invention "canned theater," and they despised and looked down on it. They considered working on a film set a dishonorable thing. A stage actor would never stoop to that kind of work unless he was desperate for money. Even if he had no choice but to make a movie, he would do it secretly, keeping it a secret from his friends, afraid of being looked down upon. However, later, these people who moved on the screen were discovered by the audience, and their status gradually became important. So, in essence, stars, whether it was Garbo, Crawford, Hepburn, or Mae West, were all created by the audience.

When moving pictures were first invented, everyone was amazed just to see things moving. But later, the audience couldn't just be satisfied with seeing shadows move. They wanted to see something more interesting than just movement. What they discovered was not the camera angles or the filming techniques, etc. What they discovered were the characters in the movies. At first, you didn't know who any of the actors were. Later, you gradually began to inquire who that girl with the long, curly hair (Mary Pickford) was. More and more people inquired, and finally, the producers realized that the names of the characters in the movies were also important. This was the beginning of the "Star System" (Star System).

But stubborn producers, even after they realized the importance of the characters, still insisted for many years on trying to get rid of that system. They said that the director's position was much more important than the actors'. They wanted to promote the director's name. Of course, the directors' contributions to the success of a film are undeniable, but somehow, the audience insisted on knowing the actors' names and placed the director's name in the optional category. The producers also wanted to promote the films themselves. They spent huge sums of money to purchase literary masterpieces and stage successes, and they hired famous writers to write the scripts. But no matter what, you, the audience, still demanded every day to know the names of every important actor. The producers couldn't resist you. They were conquered by you. By 1910, the star system was at its peak. Each and every great actor was called a "star" (To be continued)

Film Reviews

Review of "Here Comes the Navy" 336

— You Jing

Here Comes the Navy

丨 Grand Theater

Judging from the translated title "Here Comes the Navy," some people might think that this is a demonstration of maritime hegemony, a work about fierce sea battles and "killing until the ghosts cry and the gods wail." But this is just a mediocre story of a sailor's romance, a coincidence, and a chance.

While repairing the USS Arizona in the shipyard, worker Gus has a quarrel with Petty Officer Biff of the same ship. He also loses his lover in a dancing competition duel over a woman.

In order to fight for so-called "heroic spirit" in front of the woman and his rival, he joins the Navy recruitment team for military training, and as a result, he is assigned as a sailor under his rival.

The play unfolds from the point that Gus accidentally meets a girl, Rosanne, who happens to be Biff's sister. This leads to many love disputes. In the midst of Gus's aversion to the depressing mood of the Navy life, a shooting exercise occurs, and the so-called dramatic crisis of an explosion in the turret arises. Then, Gus somehow puts out the fire with his body. The play shifts to balloons through scenes of injury, awards, and job changes.

As the balloon descends, sailors from the USS Arizona rush to help. A sudden storm forms the climax of the play, ending with Gus risking his life to save Biff, fulfilling his long-cherished wish to marry Rosanne.

Here, the inadequacy of the screenwriter's technique is visible everywhere. For example, the fact that Gus happens to be assigned under Biff and that Rosanne happens to be Biff's sister are all assumed to be coincidences that the author painstakingly manages for the development of the play. The ending, with the sudden storm and Gus saving Biff, plus the fact that the fire in the powder magazine can be extinguished with the body, and the fact that the balloon completely loses its lifting and lowering function in the wind, all use illogical scenes as the key.

The producer's intention in making this film is probably to insert sailors' erotic lives, such as dancing and dueling for women, into the great warships, strict military discipline, and thrilling balloons, just to give the audience a change of pace.

Director Lloyd Bacon is quite commendable for being able to turn this script into the success it is on screen. He compensates for many of the screenwriter's shortcomings with a relaxed tone, bright shots, and witty dialogue. The performance of ninety days of military training and the depiction of sailors' erotic lives, wiping cannons, flying balls, duels, weddings, and other scenes are quite beautiful and lovely.

The camera angles and positions are also very appropriate.

Review of "Death on the Diamond" 337

— Ling He

Death on the Diamond

丨 Nanjing

Naturally, the audience needs stimulation, so American screenwriters are doing their best to find subjects in this area, and this is not without reason. But how do their screenwriters choose stimulating subjects? In the past, we have seen many works with horse racing, boxing, and boat racing as backgrounds, and now there is this "Death on the Diamond," which combines murder mystery and baseball.

In terms of artistic evaluation, "Death on the Diamond" can be said to have nothing valuable to offer except for the so-called suspenseful scenes.

In terms of the structure of the story, it cannot be said that it does not have relatively rigorous techniques. That is to say, the development of the story is relatively natural and compact. For example, the several murders of players create a rather tense atmosphere, which cannot but be determined by the script. But this is nothing more than a display of technique. The exaggeration of technique without content or principle cannot give the audience a deeper impression after all.

What does "Death on the Diamond" tell us? A baseball team, because it is used as a tool for gamblers to gamble, the players are killed one after another, and the murderer is an old man who has been with the captain for many years. He is tempted by money and is executed by law. In terms of theme, it seems to be against baseball being used as a tool for gambling, and it also carries a bit of human relationships. However, regarding the former, baseball, like horse racing and jai alai, has the same function, which is an inevitable phenomenon of capitalism. The latter is also determined by the private economic system, but the author does not explain it from this point of view. On the whole, it is an ordinary work after all.

A Casual Discussion of "Orphan of the Valley" 339

— Huo

...For thousands of years, Chinese women, under the heavy pressure of feudalism, have not been liberated and have been imprisoned in dark families all day long, living miserable lives under the iron hooves of their parents-in-law. Hu Die in "Orphan of the Valley" is a woman living in such a family, suffering misfortune. When she moves and acts on her wedding night, she is laughed at by those elders of noble families, which leads to various tragedies. This is an ethical and family problem film.

...Yan Yuexian has always played villains in films, and this time in "Orphan of the Valley" is no exception. When she dotes on her own son and abuses the children of her husband's ex-wife, that sinister expression is played vividly. The sin of this stepmother moves Hu Die to tears, which is of course one of the successful shots in "Orphan of the Valley."

...Japanese imperialism destroys our mountains and rivers. Gao Zhanfei and Zhao Dan are both members of the volunteer army. When Zhao Dan dies in battle, Gao Zhanfei cries bitterly while caressing the body. His tears really fall down. According to Lao Gao, this shot is a scene from the battlefield when he was a soldier a few years ago. No wonder Lao Gao is so sad. (True)

Film Novel

The Policeman Turns Dragon (White Lies) (6) 342

— Xin Zhi

Since Dan Oliver escaped, he has not been captured for a long time. Although the police have sent out detectives, they have not found any clues and have no way to arrest him. One morning, Joan was reading the newspaper at home when she suddenly heard someone walking outside the door. She looked up and saw that the person coming in was the ragged, haggard woman she had seen in court before. She saw Joan and asked, "Are you Joan Mitchell? I am Dan Oliver's woman, Mary Mallory. I've come... to tell you that Oliver didn't mean to hit Captain Camden. He really had no way out and was desperate. I also want to tell you that Oliver is not as bad as the Express says he is. He is just a little weak-willed. But since the Express announced his affairs, he has had no way to start over." Mary then told Joan all the things that had happened before, how she had helped him fight and waited for him to pay off his debts. Finally, Joan found out that Mary was penniless and had no place to live. Joan admired her for being so loyal to Oliver, so she told Mary that she would find her a place to live first. Mary refused at first, but Joan insisted on helping her.

After Mary left, Joan went out to find a house for Mary. She also asked Axel to help her. Later, they found a very suitable house. They paid the rent, told the landlady that they were renting it for a friend, and asked the landlady for the key. They wrote down the address and sent someone to Mary's old place. But the landlady didn't believe what Joan said, that it was rented for a friend. Joan was also busy buying a lot of food and supplies for Mary, piling them up in the house, and she was busy until dusk before she finished. Axel was already impatient and kept urging Joan to go back. Unexpectedly, just as they were about to leave the place, someone suddenly knocked on the door. Joan opened the door and saw that it was not Mary standing at the door, but Dan Oliver. Oliver first ran to Mary's old place to find her. Mary told him how righteous Mitchell's daughter was, willing to help her, and had already found a house and sent the key to her. Oliver listened and became suspicious, so he came to see what was going on. When he saw Joan, he asked her head-on, "What tricks are you playing? I'm telling you! Don't try to harm Mary Oliver!" Joan said, "We just want to help her. And I've already promised her that I'll talk to my father tonight." Oliver gnashed his teeth and said, "Oh, that's right. You're all the same. Tonight, you'll talk to your father, and then you'll send someone to catch Mary, right? I'll tell you, you can't escape!" As he said this, he stretched out his fist and knocked Joan to the ground with one punch. Axel immediately jumped up, but Oliver had already pulled out his gun and aimed it at Axel's chest. With a clang, Axel fell to the ground and died. Oliver laughed crazily, stuffed the gun into the hands of the unconscious Joan lying on the ground, and ran away.

It wasn't until dawn the next day that Joan woke up slowly. But when she saw the situation around her, she almost fainted again. She was holding a gun in her hand, and Axel was dead beside her. Her head was aching, but she struggled to run to the phone and made a call to Tyler Camden. A moment later, Camden arrived in a police car. When Joan saw him, she leaned on his shoulder and told him what she could remember, intermittently, and Camden said. She only remembered that Oliver suddenly walked in, threatened her, and then she woke up and Axel was dead beside her. After she finished speaking, she asked Camden to send her home. But Camden's face was ashen as he said, "Joan! I can't send you home. Under the law, and according to all the evidence, I have to detain you. You are suspected of murder." (To be continued)
